Free software development kits are available for Mac and Windows can be downloaded from Apple.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Device plugins allow support for additional music player devices, but the <a href="/wiki/Application_programming_interface" title="Application programming interface">APIs</a> are only licensed to authentic <a href="/wiki/Original_equipment_manufacturer" title="Original equipment manufacturer">OEMs</a> who sign a <a href="/wiki/Non-disclosure_agreement" title="Non-disclosure agreement">non-disclosure agreement</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple Inc.</a> also offers a free iOS application, Remote, that allows the user to remotely control their iTunes library or <a href="/wiki/Apple_TV" title="Apple TV">Apple TV</a> over <a href="/wiki/Digital_Audio_Control_Protocol" title="Digital Audio Control Protocol">DACP</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> This can be downloaded from iTunes itself or directly from one's iOS device. It is only compatible with iOS 7.0 and above.</p>
<p>Though iTunes itself can be installed where the user desires on Windows, ancillary applications such as Bonjour, which are part of the iTunes installation, cannot be placed in a user-desired directory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a> licensed <a href="/wiki/SoundSpectrum" title="SoundSpectrum">G-Force</a> for use in iTunes in 2001, and again in 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> This included many different WaveShapes, ColorMaps, and FlowFields; however, these configs may not be available in some versions of G-Force, although they can be found by downloading various zip files.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-extra-configs_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-extra-configs-98">[98]</a></sup> With iTunes 8.0 and later, which introduced a new visualizer, the option to select the iTunes Classic Visualizer is available in the Visualizer menu, and remains available in later versions of iTunes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thread-forum_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-thread-forum-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ITunes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Privacy_policy">Privacy policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ITunes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Privacy policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In June 2010, Apple updated its general privacy policy for the iTunes Store and iOS 4 supported devices, revealing that it could and would collect real-time location-based information on users aged 13 and over.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-http:.2F.2Fwww.apple.com.2Fprivacy_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-http:.2F.2Fwww.apple.com.2Fprivacy-100">[100]</a></sup> The information had been included in various device-specific <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EULA" title="EULA">EULAs</a> since 2008, but was not included in Apple's general privacy policy until 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>The revised policy states that Apple has the right to share this information with 3rd parties who provide services to the customer, including advertising and promotion services. Apple also states that "it may be necessary" to provide this [real-time] information in response to "requests from public and governmental authorities within or outside your country of residence or if [Apple] determines that for purposes of national security, law enforcement, or other issues of public importance, disclosure is necessary or appropriate.... Additionally, in the event of a reorganization, merger, or sale we may transfer any and all personal information we collect to the relevant third party."</p>
<p>The revised policy does not make any distinction between warrant-based and warrantless searches, nor provide what criteria would trigger the sharing of personal real-time information with government entities, nor allow an opt-out for the location-based information.</p>
<p>The revised policy prompted the co-chairs of the Bi-Partisan Privacy Caucus of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">United States House of Representatives</a> to request that Apple respond to nine basic privacy questions out of concern of possible violation of that country's Federal Communications Act. The Caucus stated it was pleased with Apple's prompt written explanations, and stated they would continue to monitor the issue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-http:.2F.2Fwww.apple.com.2Fprivacy_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-http:.2F.2Fwww.apple.com.2Fprivacy-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Security">Security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ITunes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Telegraph</a></i> reported in November 2011 that Apple had been aware of a security flaw since 2008, that would let unauthorized third parties install "updates" to end-user's iTunes' software.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TheTelegraph2011-11-28_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-TheTelegraph2011-11-28-103">[103]</a></sup> They reported that a security writer named <a href="/wiki/Brian_Krebs" title="Brian Krebs">Brian Krebs</a> had informed Apple of the vulnerability in 2008. They reported that the flaw was only closed in November 2011. They reported that <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> security software firm <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gamma_International" title="Gamma International">Gamma International</a> developed a program named <a href="/wiki/FinFisher" title="FinFisher">FinFisher</a>, intended to covertly spy on computer users, which can be clandestinely installed via bogus updates to iTunes' software. <i><a href="/wiki/Der_Spiegel" title="Der Spiegel">Der Spiegel</a></i> reported Gamma International had advertised the capability to clandestinely install FinFisher by exploiting this iTunes vulnerability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DerSpiegel2011-11-22_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-DerSpiegel2011-11-22-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Software_bloat">Software bloat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ITunes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Software bloat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>iTunes has been accused of being bloated as part of its efforts to turn it from a program that plays media to an e-commerce and advertising platform,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> with former <a href="/wiki/PC_World" title="PC World">PC World</a> editor Ed Bott accusing the company of hypocrisy in its advertising attacks on Windows for similar practices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> However, other commentators contest that criticism, saying that iTunes isn't bloated, it is just feature-rich.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="System_requirements">System requirements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ITunes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: System requirements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The following is for the newest version of iTunes.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mac">Mac</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ITunes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Mac">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl>
<dt>Hardware</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>Mac computer with an Intel Core Processor (Version 10.6.3 and earlier will run on PowerPC Processors)</li>
<li>Intel Core 2 Duo 2.0 GHz or faster processor is required to play Standard Definition video from the iTunes Store</li>
<li>2.0 GHz Intel Core 2 Duo is required to play HD video, an iTunes LP, or iTunes Extras from the iTunes Store</li>
<li>512 MB of RAM; 1 GB is required to play HD video, an iTunes LP, or iTunes Extras</li>
<li>Screen resolution of 1024×768 or greater; 1280×800 or greater is required to play an iTunes LP or iTunes Extras</li>
<li>Playing videos also requires at least 16 MB of video RAM</li>
<li>Broadband Internet connection to use the iTunes Store</li>
<li>Apple combo drive or SuperDrive to create audio, MP3, or back-up CDs; some non-Apple CD-RW recorders may also work.</li>
<li>Apple SuperDrive to back up library to DVDs; some non-Apple DVD-RW drives may also work.</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dt>Software</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>OS X 10.9.5 Mavericks or later<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></li>
<li>400 MB of available disk space</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Windows">Windows</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ITunes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Windows">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl>
<dt>Hardware</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>A PC with a 1 GHz Intel or AMD processor or Compatible CPU</li>
<li>Intel Pentium D or faster processor is required to play Standard Definition video from the iTunes Store</li>
<li>2.0 GHz Intel Core 2 Duo or faster processor is required to play HD video, an iTunes LP, or iTunes Extras from the iTunes Store</li>
<li>512 MB of RAM; 1 GB is required to play HD video, an iTunes LP, or iTunes Extras</li>
<li>Screen resolution of 1024×768 or greater; 1280×800 or greater is required to play an iTunes LP or iTunes Extras</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/DirectX" title="DirectX">DirectX</a> 9.0-compatible video card with 32 MB of video RAM; 64 MB recommended</li>
<li>Broadband Internet connection to use the iTunes Store</li>
<li>iTunes-compatible CD or DVD recorder to create audio CDs, MP3 CDs, or back-up CDs or DVDs</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dt>Software</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>32-bit editions of <a href="/wiki/Windows_7" title="Windows 7">Windows 7</a>, <a href="/wiki/Windows_8" title="Windows 8">Windows 8</a>, <a href="/wiki/Windows_8.1" title="Windows 8.1">Windows 8.1</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Windows_10" title="Windows 10">Windows 10</a></li>
<li>64-bit editions of <a href="/wiki/Windows_7" title="Windows 7">Windows 7</a>, <a href="/wiki/Windows_8" title="Windows 8">Windows 8</a>, <a href="/wiki/Windows_8.1" title="Windows 8.1">Windows 8.1</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Windows_10" title="Windows 10">Windows 10</a> require the iTunes 64-bit installer (See note)</li>
<li>400 MB of available disk space</li>
<li>Screen reader support requires <a href="/wiki/Window-Eyes" title="Window-Eyes">Window-Eyes</a> 7.1.1 or later</li>
</ul>
<p>Note: Although iTunes will operate with Windows 10, there is an issue if Windows 7 or Windows 8.1 is updated to Windows 10.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> The iPhone/iPad/iPod USB driver is disabled following the update. Often the only solution is to perform a clean install of Windows.</p>
